## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator problem where acceleration (dv/dt) is determined by restoring forces (function of x), damping forces (function of v), and possibly external driving forces (function of t). Nonlinearity introduces higher-order terms in x and/or v beyond the standard linear oscillator.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Full Duffing with quintic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (linear with periodic driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear restoring + driving)
- Driven Van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (nonlinear damping + driving)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (position-dependent stiffness)
- Quadratic-cubic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * x**2 (mixed nonlinear terms)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillation symmetry
- Even-power terms in position (x²) → asymmetric potential indicating broken spatial symmetry
- Velocity-position coupling terms like x²·v → amplitude-dependent damping (van der Pol type self-excitation)
- Cubic position terms with opposite sign to linear term → bounded motion with hardening or softening spring behavior
- Periodic time dependence cos(c·t) or sin(c·t) → externally driven oscillator with possible resonance
- Odd powers of velocity (v, v³) → dissipative forces that oppose motion direction
- Product terms x·v → phase-space-dependent forces indicating non-conservative or parametric effects
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system where energy considerations constrain the form
